          <span class="cat-links"><a href="https://www.scrapehero.com/category/scraping-tips/" rel="category tag">Scraping Tips</a></span>
         </div>
         <h1 itemprop="name" class="entry-title">How to prevent getting blacklisted while scraping</h1>
        </header>
        <div class="entry-content" itemprop="articleBody">
         <h3>Web scraping helps turn the massive amount of largely unstructured text on the web into structured data.</h3>
         <h3>It helps derive exponential better uses from the original data.</h3>
         <h3><span></span><span></span><span></span> Imagine a life without Google, because Google also uses web scraping/crawling to get almost all its data. Without Google and web scraping, we would never find all the wonderful sites and information and the Internet would not be as indispensable as it is today.</h3>
         <p><span></span><span></span><span></span>However, web scraping has to be performed responsibly so that it is does not have a detrimental effect on the sites being scraped.</p>
         <p><span></span><span></span><span></span>Web Crawlers can retrieve data much quicker, in greater depth than humans, so bad scraping practices can have some impact on the performance of the site.<br> If a crawler performs multiple requests per second and downloads large files, an under-powered server would have a hard time keeping up with requests from multiple crawlers.</p>
         <p><span></span><span></span><span></span>Since web crawlers, scrapers or spiders (words used interchangeably) dont really drive human website traffic and seemingly affect the performance of the site, some site administrators do not like spiders and try to block their access.</p>
         <p><strong>In this article, we will go through how websites detect and block spiders and talk about techniques to overcome those barriers.</strong></p>
         <p>Most websites may not have anti scraping mechanisms since it would affect the user experience, but some sites do block scraping because they do not believe in open data access.</p>
         <h2>HOW CAN WEBSITES DETECT WEB SCRAPING?</h2>
         <p><span></span><span></span><span></span>Websites can use&nbsp;different mechanisms to detect a scraper/spider from a normal user. Some of these methods are enumerated below:</p>
         <ol>
          <li>Unusual traffic/high download rate especially from a single client/or IP address within a short time span.</li>
          <li><span></span><span></span><span></span>Repetitive tasks performed on the website  based on an assumption that a human user wont perform the&nbsp;same repetitive tasks all the time.</li>
          <li><span></span><span></span><span></span>Detection through honeypots  these honeypots are usually links which arent visible to a normal user but only to a spider. When a scraper/spider tries to access the link, the alarms are tripped.</li>
         </ol>
         <p><strong><span></span><span></span><span></span>How to address this detection:<br> </strong><span></span><span></span><span></span>Spend some time upfront and investigate&nbsp;the anti-scraping mechanisms used by a site and build the spider accordingly, it will provide a better outcome in the long run and increase the longevity and robustness of your work.</p>
         <h3>EASIEST WAY TO FIND IF A SITE DOESNT WANT DATA TO BE SCRAPED</h3>
         <p>Check the robots.txt file, which is usually in the root directory of a website e.g http://example.com/robots.txt.<br> <span></span><span></span><span></span> If it contains lines like the ones shown below, it means the site doesnt like and want scraping.</p>
         <p><span></span><span></span><span></span>However, since most sites want to be on Google (arguably the largest scraper of websites globally ;-)) they do allow access to bots and spiders.</p>
         <pre>User-agent: *
Disallow: /
</pre>
         <p>This line is for preventing well-behaved bots or the bots which respect robots.txt.</p>
         <h3>WHAT HAPPENS WHEN YOU GET BANNED</h3>
         <p><span></span><span></span><span></span>There are two ways to ban a webspider/webscraper  either by banning all accesses from a particular IP or by banning all accesses that use a specific id to access the server (most browsers and web spiders identify themselves whenever they request a page by user agents. Chrome browser for example uses <code><span></span><span></span><span></span>Mozilla/5.0 (X11; Linux x86_64) AppleWebKit/537.36 (KHTML, like Gecko) Chrome/33.0.1750.149 Safari/537.36</code></p>
         <p><span></span><span></span><span></span>The banning can be temporary or permanent. Temporary blocks can last minutes or hours. Permanent bans go against the open nature of the Internet but some sites resort to this scorch the internet measure.</p>
         <h2>HOW DO YOU FIND OUT IF A SITE HAS BLOCKED YOU?</h2>
         <p>If any of the following symptoms appear on the site that you are crawling, it is usually a sign of being blocked or banned.</p>
         <ul>
          <li>CAPTCHA&nbsp;pages</li>
          <li>Unusual content delivery delay</li>
          <li>Frequent response with HTTP 404, 301 or 50x errors</li>
         </ul>
         <p><span></span><span></span><span></span>also frequent appearance of these status codes is also indication of blocking</p>
         <ul>
          <li>301 Moved Temporarily</li>
          <li>401 Unauthorized</li>
          <li>403 Forbidden</li>
          <li>404 Not Found</li>
          <li>408 Request Timeout</li>
          <li>429 Too Many Requests</li>
          <li>503 Service Unavailable</li>
         </ul>
         <p><span></span><span></span><span></span>A comprehensive list of HTTP return codes (successes and failures) can be found <a href="http://www.w3.org/Protocols/rfc2616/rfc2616-sec10.html">here</a>. It will be worth your time to read through these codes and be familiar with them.</p>
         <h1>WEB CRAWLING BEST PRACTICES</h1>
         <h2>Rule 1  Be Nice</h2>
         <p>An overarching rule to keep in mind for any kind of web scraping is</p>
         <blockquote>
          <p><span></span><span></span><span></span>BE GOOD AND FOLLOW A WEBSITES CRAWLING POLICIES</p>
         </blockquote>
         <p>Here are some of the best practices you can follow to overcome the detection.</p>
         <h3>1. MAKE THE CRAWLING SLOWER, DO NOT SLAM THE SERVER, TREAT THEM NICELY</h3>
         <p>Use auto throttling mechanisms which will automatically throttle the crawling speed based on the load on both the spider and the website that you are crawling. Adjust the spider to an optimum crawling speed after a few trial runs and do this periodically because the environment does change over time.</p>
         <p>The faster you crawl, the worse it is for everyone.</p>
         <p>Put some random programmatic sleep calls in between requests, add some delays after crawling a small number of pages and choose the lowest number of concurrent requests possible.</p>
         <p>These techniques make the spider look like a human and are generally good for everyone.</p>
         <h3>2. DISGUISE YOUR REQUESTS BY ROTATING IPs and PROXY SERVICES</h3>
         <p><span></span><span></span><span></span>A server can easily detects a bot by checking the requests from a single IP address, so if you use different IP addresses for making requests to a server, the detection becomes harder. Create a pool of IPs that you&nbsp;can use and use random ones for each request.<br> <span></span><span></span><span></span> There are several methods can be used to change your outgoing IP.<br> <span></span><span></span><span></span> Services such as VPNs, shared proxies and TOR can help. In addition, various commercial providers also provide services for automatic IP rotation.</p>
         <p>This technique also distributes the load across various exit points.</p>
         <p><span></span><span></span><span></span>Some websites have blocked well known IP ranges such as AWS completely to prevent using the massive Amazon AWS IPs. Such protectionist policies are obviously counter to the open nature of the Internet.</p>
         <h3>3. USER-AGENT ROTATION AND SPOOFING</h3>
         <p><span></span><span></span><span></span>Every request made from a web browser contains a user-agent header and using the same user-agent consistently leads to&nbsp;the detection of a bot.</p>
         <p>User Agent rotation and spoofing is the best solution for this.</p>
         <p><span></span><span></span><span></span>Spoof the User Agent by creating a list of user agents and picking a random one for each request.<br> <span></span><span></span><span></span> Websites do not want to block genuine users so you should try to look like one. Set your user-agent to a common web browser instead of using the default user-agent (such as wget/version or urllib/version). You could even pretend to be the Google Bot: Googlebot/2.1 if you want to have some fun! (<a href="http://www.google.com/bot.html">http://www.google.com/bot.html</a>)</p>
         <p>You can check your user-agent string here:<br> <a href="http://wiht.link/wmuseragent">http://www.whatsmyuseragent.com/</a></p>
         <p><span></span><span></span><span></span>A user-agent string listing to get you started can be found&nbsp;here:<br> <a href="http://www.useragentstring.com/pages/useragentstring.php">http://www.useragentstring.com/pages/useragentstring.php</a></p>
         <p>A nice python based library to make this rotation easier is <a href="https://pypi.python.org/pypi/fake-useragent">Fake User Agent</a>.</p>
         <h3><span></span><span></span><span></span>4. BEWARE OF HONEYPOTS</h3>
         <p><span></span><span></span><span></span>Some websites install honeypots to detect web spiders. These honeypots usually are links that normal user cant see but a spider can.<br> When following links always take care that the link has proper visibility with no <strong><span></span><span></span><span></span>nofollow</strong><span></span><span></span><span></span> tag. Some&nbsp;honeypot links to detect spiders will be have the CSS style&nbsp;<strong>display:none</strong> or will be color disguised to blend in with the pages background color.</p>
         <p><span></span><span></span><span></span>This detection is obviously not easy and requires a significant amount of programming work to accomplish properly, as a result this technique is not widely used on either side  the server side or the bot or scraper side.</p>
         <h3>5. DO NOT FOLLOW THE SAME CRAWLING PATTERN</h3>
         <p>Only robots follow the same crawling pattern because unless specified otherwise, programmed bots follow a logic which is usually very specific.</p>
         <p><span></span><span></span><span></span>Sites that have intelligent anti-crawling mechanisms can easily detect spiders from finding pattern in their actions. Humans generally will not perform&nbsp;repetitive tasks.</p>
         <p>Incorporate&nbsp;some random clicks on the page, mouse movements and random actions that will&nbsp;make a spider looks like a human.</p>
         <h3>6. ALWAYS RESPECT THE<span style="color: #ff0000;">&nbsp;robots.txt <span style="color: #000000;">FILE</span><br> </span></h3>
         <p><span></span><span></span><span></span>Web spiders should ideally follow rules in a robots.txt file for the website being scraped. The robots.txt file specifies rules for good behavior, such as how frequently bots are allowed to request pages, what pages are allowed to be scraped and which areas are off limits for scraping.</p>
         <p>However, some websites are extremely liberal with letting Google scrape their websites but not allowing any other bots access. This goes against the open nature of the Internet, but the websites owners are well within their rights to resort to such behavior.</p> [Update July 11 2017: Added new item below]
         <h3>7. USE A HEADLESS BROWSER<span><br> </span></h3>
         <p><span></span><span></span><span></span>Some websites present different content based on the type of browser that is accessing the site. The Google search results is a perfect example of such behavior. If the browser (identified by the user agent) has advanced capabilities, the website may present richer content  something more dynamic and styled which may have a heavy reliance on Javascript and CSS. Some websites may also use the same Javascript based methods to detect the browser capabilities despite the user agent that is advertised by the bot. e.g. if the browser identifies itself as a Chrome 50 version (which definitely has Javascript support), the website can use some script based programming to identify whether the browser can actually perform some client-side calculation.</p>
         <p><span></span>The solution for this is to use headless browsers (browsers that arent really visual on a desktop but are fully functional otherwise). <a href="http://www.seleniumhq.org/">Selenium</a>, <a href="http://phantomjs.org/"><span></span><span></span><span></span>PhantomJS</a>, and the latest entrant  Googles own headless <a href="https://developers.google.com/web/updates/2017/04/headless-chrome">chrome </a>are some options to explore further.</p>
         <p>Keep in mind that headless browsers use a lot of resources (RAM, CPU, Bandwidth etc) in comparison to script based approaches.</p>
         <h2>Summary</h2>
         <p><span></span><span></span><span></span>All these ideas above provide a starting point for you to build your own solutions or refine your existing solution. If you have any ideas or suggestions, please join the discussion in the comments section.</p>
         <p>Thank you for reading.</p>
         <p><span></span><span></span><span></span></p>
